item_7.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-1388]. Client: Sariya Mason.

In the matter captioned Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo, et al. (Jefferson Circuit Court of Kentucky, case number 23-CI-006039), a correspondence thread was logged among counsel in early and mid-2025. On June 3, 2025, at 12:41:59 p.m. Eastern Time, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to counsel Matthew Londergan and Deanna Tucker, with Kristy M. King and the Filevine project email address for Sariya Mason copied on the message. The subject line reflected the Schrice Thomas v. Castillo matter, and Koon stated in the body, “Good afternoon counsel, Please see attached filed today and set for Monday's motion hour.” He signed with his full contact details for The Whaley Law Firm: 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-28]; fax [PHONE-1386]. The email carried a standard attorney‑client confidentiality disclaimer, noting that the message is intended only for the named recipient, may contain privileged information, and that if it was received in error the recipient should contact The Whaley Law Firm and refrain from using or forwarding the material.

Earlier in the thread, on May 20, 2025, at approximately 10:01 a.m. (the timestamp shown as “10:01?AM” in the record), Koon wrote to the same recipients: “Good afternoon counsel, Just wanted to follow up on this one. Thanks.” This message also carried The Whaley Law Firm’s signature block and the same confidentiality disclaimer.

Prior to that, on May 12, 2025, at about 9:54 a.m. (noted as “9:54?AM” in the record), Koon sent another message: “Good afternoon counsel, Before moving forward, I wanted to check in to see if you’re open to mediation or continuing informal settlement talks. It might make sense to see if we can get this resolved before putting more time and resources into it. Let me know what you think.” This message likewise included the firm’s contact information and the standard confidentiality notice.

In all three messages, the confidentiality disclaimer appears at the end, stating that the electronic message is intended only for the named recipient and may contain attorney‑client privileged or protected information; if received in error, the recipient should contact The Whaley Law Firm, there is no waiver of privilege, and the information should not be used or forwarded to anyone not intended to receive it.

item_13.note: Case note for client Sariya Mason concerns depositions in the matter of Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo et al., Jeff Cir Crt, case number 23-CI-006039. The depositions were being coordinated between The Whaley Law Firm and SBMKY Law, with communications involving W. Bryce Koon, Esq. (The Whaley Law Firm), Kristy M. King (Legal Assistant at SBMKY Law), Sarena Tuttle (Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm), Matthew Londergan (SBMKY), and Deanna M. Tucker (SBMKY). The depositions were ultimately scheduled for April 29, 2025, at 10:00 a.m., to be held at Kristy M. King’s office at 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, Kentucky 40202. The note records that the clients were to attend, and that the depositions were set to proceed as soon as possible to avoid further delays, noting that the claim had been pending for nearly three years and that video evidence existed showing how the incident unfolded.

The chronology begins with scheduling discussions in early 2025. On February 11, 2025, Kristy M. King asked if a 10:00 a.m. start at SBMKY’s office would be acceptable for the plaintiffs’ depositions. Later that same day, Sarena Tuttle replied affirmatively, indicating “Absolutely,” and noting that they had just heard back from Mrs. Thomas. Kristy followed with a confirmation that the 10:00 a.m. start at SBMKY’s office would be suitable, and Sarena acknowledged with a brief positive reply. The February 11 exchanges also included standard confidentiality language typical of such communications.

The scheduling discussion continued on March 17, 2025, reflecting an initial scheduling conflict. Kristy M. King advised that Mr. Londergan was available on April 29, 30, and May 1, and asked for preferences regarding dates or a start time. Sarena Tuttle responded that the early April timeframe was difficult due to Spring Break and vacations, but that they could consider the week after Easter, listing open dates of April 22, 23, 24, 29, 30, or May 1 and asking which date would work best for the opponent’s office. In a follow-up, Sarena explicitly confirmed that April 29th would work for them and that they preferred a 10:00 a.m. start at the opponent’s office.

By late March, the parties had settled on April 29, 2025, at 10:00 a.m. for the plaintiffs’ depositions at Kristy King’s office. Kristy King’s March 17, 2025 messages and Sarena Tuttle’s responses reflected the agreed-upon 10:00 a.m. start and the preference to proceed on April 29 to avoid additional delays. The record also shows ongoing back-and-forth among the attorneys and staff about the scheduling, with the understanding that the depositions would proceed promptly.

On April 28, 2025, the day before the scheduled depositions, Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm confirmed with the SBMKY counterpart that the clients would be at the opposing counsel’s office the following day for their depositions at 10:00 a.m. He stated, “Good afternoon counsel, I have confirmed with my clients that we will be at your office tomorrow at 10 for their depositions.” He provided his contact information for The Whaley Law Firm at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with phone [PHONE-59] and fax [PHONE-60]. Kristy M. King replied later that afternoon to confirm the depositions for tomorrow, April 29, and asked to be informed if anything had changed. Kristy’s email signature included her title as Legal Assistant and her office address at 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, Kentucky 40202, with direct phone [PHONE-61] and direct fax [PHONE-62]. Each of these messages included standard confidentiality notices indicating the communications were intended only for the named recipients and may be protected by attorney-client or work product privileges; recipients were instructed to notify the sender and destroy the message if received in error.

In summary, the depositions in Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo et al., Jeff Cir Crt, 23-CI-006039, were scheduled and confirmed for April 29, 2025, at 10:00 a.m., at Kristy King’s office in Louisville, Kentucky. The depositions were to proceed for the plaintiffs, with the expectation of moving forward promptly to prevent further delays in a case nearing three years of duration, supported by video evidence of the incident. The communications included both the scheduling confirmations and the required confidentiality disclosures typical of attorney communications.

item_22.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-1325]
Client: Sariya Mason

This record concerns the matter Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al, in Jeff Cir Crt, case number 23-CI-006039. The deposition scheduling communications involve counsel from The Whaley Law Firm and from SBMKY Law, with the Plaintiffs Mr. Vilches, Mrs. Castillo, Mrs. Thomas, and Sariya Mason referenced in various positions in the thread. The note begins with a recent scheduling conflict raised by Kristy M. King, a legal assistant, on March 17, 2025, who asked for new dates after advising of a conflict for tomorrow and noting the need to reschedule the Plaintiffs’ depositions.

In the run-up to these dates, the calendar coordination unfolded through a sequence of emails in February 2025. On February 10, 2025, Matthew R. Londergan, an attorney with the Whaley/Belmont group, requested that the two depositions—those of Ms. Thomas and Sariya—be scheduled in the same timeframe and asked for dates in March or April that would work for the counsel and the Plaintiffs. The response from Sarena M. Tuttle was prompt. She indicated “Absolutely” and sent back information, noting that the firm had attached the NTTD (Notice to Take Depositions) for the Defendant’s Depositions and that a Spanish translator was being requested for that day. She also said she had asked Mrs. Thomas and Sariya to check their availability and that she would provide updates as soon as she heard back.

Earlier in the day, there was an initial note from Sarena replying “Awesome” to the request, followed by further detail in the subsequent communications. Also on February 10, 2025, Sarena referenced that Kristy had asked whether a 10:00 a.m. start at SBMKY’s office would be suitable for the depositions.

The thread then shows a key development on February 11, 2025. Matthew Londergan informed Sarena that they had learned Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6. Ms. Castillo would still be available on that date, and the two depositions could be conducted on the same day if desired. The teams confirmed that Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo would be available at any time on any of the following days: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, and March 27. A conference room at their office was also available on these dates. They noted that if none of these dates worked for the other office, April dates could be considered.

In response to the proposed dates, Sarena advised that they could move the deposition to March 13 without issue. Matthew responded that they would inform their clients. Sarena then noted that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya had responded and would be available on March 18, 2025. Kristy asked for confirmation about a 10:00 a.m. start at their office for the depositions, and Sarena replied with “Awesome,” confirming readiness to proceed under that arrangement.

Across these exchanges, the communications repeatedly referenced confidentiality notices attached to each email and the need to handle discovery with attorney-client/work product privileges preserved.

By February 11, 2025, the parties had established potential dates on which both Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo could be deposed (March 13, 18, 20, 25, or 27), with arrangements for a conference room at the defense office if needed, and with the additional detail that a Spanish translator would be requested for the day. The availability updates indicated that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available on March 18, 2025, and that the 10:00 a.m. start at the defense office was being considered.

On March 17, 2025, Kristy M. King sent a new email noting a scheduling conflict for tomorrow and requesting that additional dates be provided that would work for both counsel and the Plaintiffs, Sariya Mason and Mrs. Thomas, in order to reschedule the Plaintiffs’ depositions. She asked for alternative dates and apologized for the late notice.

In summary, the record reflects a coordinated effort in February 2025 to schedule the depositions of the Plaintiffs in Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al., with proposed dates including March 13, 18, 20, 25, and 27, consideration of Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo’s availability, a plan to use a conference room at the defense office, and a request for a 10:00 a.m. start on the days chosen. By mid-March, a scheduling conflict prompted a request for additional date options to accommodate counsel and the Plaintiffs, including Sariya Mason and Mrs. Thomas. Throughout, confidentiality notices accompanied each message.

item_23.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-1323]. Client: Sariya Mason. The matter at hand is Schrice Thomas v Yanely Castillo et al., in Jeff Cir. Crt., case number 23-CI-006039. The exchange below concerns scheduling the plaintiffs’ depositions in this matter, with involvement from The Whaley Law Firm (Sarena M. Tuttle) and SBMKY Law (Kristy M. King, Matthew Londergan, and other firm personnel).

In mid-February 2025, Kristy M. King, a legal assistant at SBMKY Law in Louisville, first proposed a 10:00 a.m. start for the plaintiffs’ depositions at SBMKY’s office. The email was sent on February 11, 2025, to Sarena Tuttle at The Whaley Law Firm, with copies to Matthew Londergan and other colleagues, and included Kristy’s standard confidentiality notice. Kristy asked whether a 10:00 a.m. start at SBMKY’s office would work for the depositions.

Later that same day, Sarena replied that they could move the deposition date to the 13th without issue and also noted that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available on March 18, 2025. In the same thread, Sarena stated that they had just heard back from Mrs. Thomas, and that she and Sariya Mason would be available on March 18. Matthew Londergan replied that they would inform their clients. A fragment of the thread also indicated that Ms. Vilches would now be out of the [incomplete phrase ends here], though the exact circumstance was not fully captured in the note.

Concurrent with those exchanges, Kristy asked whether there was a preference among the dates Mr. Londergan’s schedule could accommodate for the depositions—specifically noting that Mr. Londergan was available on April 29, 30, and May 1. Sarena hadn’t yet fixed a date beyond March 18, but she later responded that April 29 could work for them, and she and Mr. Londergan discussed the preferred start time.

On February 11, 2025, after Kristy’s initial scheduling inquiry, Sarena followed up again, indicating that they could move the depositions to the 13th if needed and confirming that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya would be available on March 18, 2025. Shortly thereafter, Matthew Londergan confirmed that they would notify their clients of the proposed dates.

By mid-March, scheduling tensions resurfaced as Kristy reported a conflict for the following day and requested additional dates that would work for counsel and Plaintiffs. Sarena acknowledged the conflict and explained that early April would be tricky due to Spring Break and vacations, but she proposed looking at the week after Easter with open dates including April 22, 23, 24, 29, 30, or May 1. Kristy then asked for a preference among the dates of April 29, 30, or May 1, as those were the days Mr. Londergan was available, and she inquired about a preferred start time.

Sarena responded that April 29, 2025 was fine for them, noting that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available on that date, and she reminded that Mr. Londergan was available on April 29, 30, and May 1. Kristy confirmed the readline about dates and asked if there was a preferred start time. In response, Sarena reiterated that April 29 was acceptable for their side and that they would proceed accordingly, reaffirming their availability.

On March 17, 2025, Kristy confirmed the plan and stated that she would issue an Amended Notice. Specifically, Kristy wrote, Sounds good. I’ll get an Amended Notice out. This marked the intended formalization of the agreed deposition schedule.

Throughout the thread, each email included the standard confidentiality notices common to attorney communications, indicating the content was intended solely for the named recipients and protected by attorney-work product privileges, with instructions to notify the sender if received in error and to destroy the transmission.

In sum: the parties were coordinating depositions for Schrice Thomas v Yanely Castillo et al. (Jeff Cir Crt, 23-CI-006039), with Sariya Mason and Mrs. Thomas as plaintiffs. Initial discussions in February proposed a 10:00 a.m. start at SBMKY’s office, with March 18, 2025 as a target date for availability. Scheduling conflicts and spring break concerns followed, leading to a focus on the week after Easter and potential dates of April 22-24, 29-30, or May 1, with Mr. Londergan available on April 29, 30, and May 1. Ultimately, on March 17, 2025, Kristy King indicated she would issue an Amended Notice to reflect the agreed schedule.

The thread begins with a February 11, 2025 exchange between The Whaley Law Firm and SBMKY Law. Kristy M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, with a cc to Matthew Londergan and Bryce Koon, and to Deanna M. Tucker and Benji Smith. Sarena’s message included her signature block and her new email address (Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com). In response, Sarena wrote, “Absolutely.” Separately, later that day Sarena noted that she and Mrs. Thomas had heard back and that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya would be available on March 18, 2025. Kristy asked for preferred dates and start times. In response, Sarena stated that Mr. Londergan was available on April 29, 30, and May 1, and asked whether there was a preference among those dates or a preferred start time.

Sarena then communicated that April 29 was acceptable and urged keeping the deposition as soon as possible to avoid further delays, noting that the claim is approaching three years and that there is video proof of how the incident unfolded. She proposed a start time of 10:00 a.m. at Kristy’s office. The message concluded with Sarena’s standard sign-off and contact details, including her updated email address.

Kristy replied that she would issue an Amended Notice. In a separate March 17 message, Sarena reiterated that the parties preferred moving forward promptly and reiterated the availability window discussed earlier. She also restated the open dates for the week after Easter: April 22, 23, 24, 29, 30, or May 1, and noted that Mr. Londergan was available on April 29, 30, and May 1, with a request for a preferred start time.

Earlier on March 17, Kristy had requested additional possible dates due to a scheduling conflict for the following day and apologized for the late notice. Sarena confirmed that April 22, 23, 24, 29, 30, or May 1 were open for consideration. The thread includes the typical confidentiality notices in each email.

The thread also reflects an earlier exchange from February 11, 2025, in which Sarena confirmed that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya would be available on March 18, 2025, and that the depositions could begin at 10:00 a.m. at the office. The notes remind readers that the communications included the parties’ respective contact details: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-97]; O: [PHONE-98] ext 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (new email address); Kristy M. King’s contact details at 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, KY 40202; Direct Phone: [PHONE-99]; Direct Fax: [PHONE-100]. Tucker (SBMKY Law), and Benji Smith (SBMKY Law). The communications were CC’d to these individuals, and the email chain contained standard confidentiality notices.

Sarena Tuttle replied that they could move the deposition to the 13th without issue. King stated that there had been a scheduling conflict for tomorrow and asked for additional dates that would work for counsel and the Plaintiffs, apologizing for the late notice. Sarena Tuttle replied that, although early April is tricky due to Spring Break and vacations, they could look at the week after Easter, with open dates of April 22, 23, 24, 29, 30, or May 1. Kristy then asked for preferences among those dates and/or a preferred start time, while the records show that April 29 was eventually selected as the agreed date.

In the final exchange documented in this note, dated March 17, 2025 at 14:21:31 -0400, Sarena stated that April 29 would work for them and that they wanted to proceed as soon as possible to avoid further delays, noting that the claim was approaching three years and that there was video proof of how the incident unfolded. She proposed a 10:00 a.m. start time at the recipient’s office. Her message was signed with her contact details: Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; Direct D: [PHONE-103]; Office: [PHONE-104] ext 104; Email: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (Please note new email address).

item_26.note: This note summarizes the scheduling communications for depositions in the case Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al., Jeff Cir Crt, 23-CI-006039, with client Sariya Mason. The involved law firms are The Whaley Law Firm (Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, and colleagues Matthew Londergan, Bryce Koon, Deanna M. Tucker, and Benji Smith) and SBM Kentucky Law ( Kristy M. King, a Legal Assistant, and Mr. Matthew Londergan as the client contact). The depositions at issue concern Plaintiffs, including Sariya Mason, and the parties have been coordinating through email exchanges that span February and March 2025. Each email contained a confidentiality notice stating that the communication and attachments are confidential and privileged and should be treated accordingly.

Beginning in mid-February 2025, the parties discussed dates for the plaintiffs’ depositions and the logistics of where and when they would occur. In a February 11 exchange, the Whaley firm advised that the depositions could be moved to March 13 without issue, and that the depositions could be held in their office with a conference room available for use on any of the proposed dates. They noted that Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6, and that Ms. Castillo would be available on that day if both depositions were desired on the same day. The Whaley team listed several potential dates for depositions: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, and March 27, with the option to reschedule into April if those dates did not work. They also indicated that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available on March 18, 2025. In addition, they proposed a 10:00 a.m. start time for the depositions at their office. Matthew Londergan acknowledged the proposed dates and noted that he would inform their clients.

Later on February 11, 2025, Matthew Londergan confirmed that Ms. Vilches would be unavailable on March 6 due to being out of the country, but that Ms. Castillo remained available on that date. He reiterated the available dates for scheduling: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, and March 27, with a conference room available at their office. He suggested that if both depositions could be held on the same day, they would coordinate accordingly. The Whaley team responded affirmatively to the 10:00 a.m. start time, and the exchange continued with further confirmations about the dates and client availability. Matthew later indicated that he would inform their clients of the proposed schedule, and Sarena replied, “Absolutely,” expressing appreciation for Kristy’s coordination.

In the same February 11 thread, there is a rapid back-and-forth about timing and client availability. The Whaley team confirmed that moving to March 13 was acceptable, and they provided the March 18 availability for Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason. They also confirmed that depositions could start at 10:00 a.m. at the SBM Kentucky office, and that a conference room would be available for the depositions. The sequence also shows ongoing coordination regarding whether both depositions should occur on the same day and how best to accommodate the calendar constraints, with the parties showing flexibility about April dates if March dates proved impractical.

By March 17, 2025, scheduling again required adjustment due to conflicts in early April. Kristy M. King conveyed that there had been a scheduling conflict for the next day and asked for additional dates that would work for counsel and the Plaintiffs. She noted that Mr. Londergan was available on April 29, 30, and May 1 and asked if there was a preferred date or start time. Kristy’s message closed with her standard confirmation and contact details. The Whaley firm replied with a plan to consider the later dates and asked for guidance on preferred times.

In response to Kristy’s March 17 message, Sarena Tuttle provided a clear set of alternative open dates in the week after Easter: April 22, 23, 24, 29, and 30, as well as May 1. She asked Kristy to indicate which of these dates would work best for her office. This offered window reflects ongoing collaborative scheduling between the two firms to finalize the depositions for the plaintiffs, including Sariya Mason and Mrs. Thomas, in this Jefferson Circuit Court case.

Additional context within the chain shows prior back-and-forth in February about possible start times (with at one point a suggested 10:00 a.m. start) and the availability of the parties. There are references to both Ms. Castillo and Ms. Vilches, and to coordinating depositions either on separate days or on the same day, with the option to move to April if March dates could not be arranged. Throughout, the discussions emphasize the need to accommodate Spring Breaks, vacations, and travel constraints, while securing a suitable conference-room space at the scheduling firm’s office.

In short, the parties have been negotiating depositions for Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al., with plaintiffs including Sariya Mason. Initial February exchanges proposed multiple March dates (including March 13, 18, 20, 25, and 27) and a 10:00 a.m. start, subject to availability of a conference room at the filing firm’s offices. Availability updates indicated that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available on March 18, and that Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6, with other days available for scheduling. By mid-March, Mr. Londergan’s availability moved to late April and early May (April 29, 30, and May 1), and Sarena offered open dates in late April and early May (April 22–24, 29–30, and May 1), requesting confirmation of which option worked best for Kristy’s office. The correspondence remains confidential and privileged, as noted in each email.

item_46.note: Case: Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al., Jefferson Circuit Court, 23-CI-006039, was the subject of a series of scheduling emails in February 2025 involving the representation for Sariya Mason (the client) and counsel for the other side. The Whaley Law Firm, on behalf of Sariya Mason, coordinated depositions in the matter with SBMKY Law. In the initial exchange, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm, sent to Kristy M. King and cc’d colleagues a notice that included an attached Notice to Take the Deposition of the Defendant (NTTD) and a request for a Spanish translator for the day, noting that she had reached out to Mrs. Thomas and Sariya to check their availability and would provide updates.

On February 10, 2025, Kristy M. King asked whether a 10:00 a.m. start at their office would be acceptable for the depositions. In reply, Sarena confirmed a positive response: “Absolutely. Thank you so much,” and signed with her updated contact information. Earlier that same day, Kristy’s team had proposed a potential schedule, and Matthew R. Londergan, an attorney for SBMKY, had asked for dates in March and April to align depositions for Ms. Thomas and Sariya.

Later on February 10, 2025, Sarena told Matthew that they could move the deposition date to the 13th without issue. The next day, February 11, 2025, Matthew informed Sarena that they had learned Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6, and that Ms. Castillo was available that day. He added that, if both depositions were to occur on the same day, they had confirmed that both Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo would be available at any time on the following dates: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, and March 27, and that a conference room would be available at their office for the depositions on any of those dates; if none of these dates worked for the other office, they could pursue dates in April. 

Sarena replied that the plan sounded good and that they would issue a notice to the court reporter that day. A subsequent message from Sarena to Matthew acknowledged the new dates, stating that moving the deposition to the 13th was not a problem. Matthew then responded, thanking her and saying they would inform their clients. Later that day, Sarena noted that they had heard back from Mrs. Thomas, who, along with Sariya Mason, would be available on March 18, 2025. Kristy then inquired about starting the depositions at 10:00 a.m. at their office, to which Sarena replied, “Absolutely. Thank you so much, Kristy,” and signed her message with her full contact information, including her new email address.

For reference, the communications included the following contact details and identifiers: Sarena M. Tuttle, The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; direct dial [PHONE-193]; office [PHONE-194] ext 104; email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (noting the new address). Kristy M. King’s office address appeared as 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, KY 40202, with direct phone [PHONE-195] and direct fax [PHONE-1219]. The depositions were to be held in the presenting firm’s conference room, with dates proposed for March 13, 18, 20, 25, and 27, and a March 6 option previously discussed due to Ms. Vilches’ travel, all subject to the availability of Mrs. Thomas (Schrice Thomas) and Sariya Mason for the day and the possible need for a Spanish translator.

item_47.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-198]. Client: Sariya Mason. This note relates to Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al., before the Jeff Cir Crt, case number 23-CI-006039. The email thread consists of communications between Matthew R. Londergan of SBMKY Law and Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, with multiple recipients on CC and by email, concerning scheduling depositions for the defendants and the related Notice to Take Deposition (NTTD), including arrangements for a Spanish translator and a suitable venue.

The exchange began in early February 2025. On February 10, 2025, Matthew Londergan asked Sarena Tuttle to propose dates in March and April for the depositions of Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo, noting that a conference room at his office would be available for the depositions. He requested that they coordinate with their clients, Ms. Thomas and Sariya Mason, and keep him posted if anything changed. The initial message included his direct contact details and a confidentiality notice typical of attorney communications.

Later on February 10, Sarena responded that they had attached the Notice to Take Depositions (NTTD) for the Defendant’s Depositions and had requested a Spanish translator for that day. She indicated that she had sent a request to Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason to check their availability and promised to update as soon as responses were received. She also provided her contact information and noted a new Whaley Law Firm email address in the chain. In a follow-up, she confirmed that they would get a notice to Matthew and the court reporter that day, reiterating the plan to coordinate the depositions.

On February 10, 2025, Matthew replied that the conference room at his office was available and that either order of depositions would be acceptable. He reiterated his willingness to accommodate the scheduling and to notify the clients accordingly. Sarena then attached the NTTD and again affirmed the availability of a Spanish translator, along with the standard confidentiality notice.

Later on February 11, 2025, Sarena indicated that they could move the depositions to March 13 without issue. In response, Matthew noted that he had learned Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6, and that while Ms. Castillo was available that day, they could schedule both depositions on the same day if desired. He reported that both Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo would be available on any of the following days: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, or March 27, and he reminded that a conference room was available at their office for the depositions. He also offered to discuss further if needed. This message thread contains the standard confidentiality notices on each email.

On February 11, 2025 at 12:59 PM, Sarena confirmed once more that they could move to March 13. At 1:22 PM, Matthew responded, “Great, thank you. We will let our clients know.” Later that same day, Sarena informed Matthew that they had just heard back from Mrs. Thomas, and that both Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available on March 18, 2025. In the final note from February 11, 2025 at 7:12 PM, Matthew thanked her and stated that they would get the depositions noticed for their office on March 18, and asked to be informed if anything changed in the meantime.

Across the thread, the parties discussed the Notice to Take Depositions, arranged for a Spanish translator, and coordinated availability for two defendants’ depositions—Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo—while reserving the office conference room for the proceedings. The stated plan, as of the latest update, is to notice the depositions for March 18, 2025, with flexibility to adjust to alternative dates (March 13, 18, 20, 25, 27) if needed, and to proceed with both depositions on the same day if feasible.

item_48.note: In the matter of Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al., Jeff Cir Crt, 23-CI-006039, the scheduling communications were exchanged in February 2025 between The Whaley Law Firm and Sariya Mason’s counsel, as part of the Sariya-Mason-DB file dated August 19, 2022. The depositions at issue involve Ms. Thomas and Sariya Mason, with defendants including Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo, and the team planned to hold the depositions at the Whaley Law Firm office.

On February 10, 2025, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm began outlining the plan. In a morning message, she stated that March 6, 2025 would begin at 10:00 a.m. with Mrs. Vilches and would continue with the other deponent. Matthew Londergan replied later that day, noting that the conference room at his office would be available that day and that Whaley could determine the deposition order. He followed up that same day by expressing readiness to send a notice to the court reporter and to coordinate with the clients.

Earlier that morning, multiple messages circulated regarding dates and coordination. Matthew asked for dates in March or April when Ms. Thomas and Sariya would be available, and Sarena attached a Notice to Take Depositions (NTTD) for the defendants’ depositions, along with a request for a Spanish translator for that day and a request for Mrs. Thomas and Sariya to confirm their availability. Kristy M. King, the legal assistant for Sariya Mason, also included a confidentiality notice in her communications.

Over the next hours, the parties discussed adjusting the schedule. Sarena indicated they could move the deposition date to March 13. Matthew noted that Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6, but that Ms. Castillo would be available that day; he also advised that if both depositions were to occur on the same day, they had confirmed that both Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo would be available on any of the following mutually workable dates: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, and March 27. The Whaley team requested flexibility on the date and reminded that a conference room would be available at their office for whichever order the depositions occurred. If none of those dates worked, they suggested moving to April.

On February 11, 2025, further updates were exchanged. An earlier message from Matthew had requested that the parties’ availability be provided for March/April, and Sarena replied that they could move the depositions to March 13. Matthew followed by confirming that Ms. Vilches would now be unavailable on March 6, but that Ms. Castillo would still be available that day; the group remained open to scheduling both depositions on the same day on one of the dates listed (March 13, 18, 20, 25, or 27), with a court reporter and a conference room arranged at the office. She noted that they would update as soon as they heard back.

Sarena then informed Matthew that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya would be available on March 18, 2025. In parallel, Kristy M. King circulated that the 10:00 a.m. start time at The Whaley Law Firm’s office was being considered for the depositions.

Throughout these exchanges, new contact details surfaced: Sarena Tuttle noted a new email address (Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com) for future correspondence, and Kristy M. King’s signature appeared with the Whaley Law Firm’s Louisville address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222) and the firm’s phone and fax numbers.

In summary, the parties coordinated multiple schedules for the depositions in Schrice Thomas v. Castillo et al., with initial plans to begin on March 6, 2025 at 10:00 a.m. (Vilches first, then Castillo), the option to conduct both depositions on the same day, and subsequent adjustments moving toward March 13 or March 18, 2025, while ensuring a court reporter, a Spanish translator, an NTTD, and a suitable conference room setting were arranged.

item_49.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-1214]. Client: Sariya Mason. This note covers communications regarding the deposition schedule in the matter Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al, Jeff Cir Court, 23-CI-006039.

On February 11, 2025, the Whaley Law Firm alerted SBMKY Law that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available for depositions on March 18, 2025. The message came from Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, and included the firm’s contact details.

Earlier in the thread, Matthew R. Londergan of SBMKY Law had indicated they would inform their clients of potential dates. In response to scheduling needs, Sarena confirmed on February 10, 2025 that the defendants’ depositions would be conducted, beginning March 6, 2025 at 10:00 a.m. with Mrs. Vilches and continuing with Mrs. Castillo, and noted that a Spanish translator had been requested for that day. She also indicated she had sent a request to Mrs. Thomas and Sariya to check their availability and would provide an update as soon as she heard back. The same day, SBMKY stated that the conference room at their office would be available for the depositions on that date, and that the order of the depositions could be arranged as Whaley preferred.

Later that day, SBMKY reiterated that the conference room would be available and that they were flexible about the order of the depositions. On February 10, 2025 at 11:23 a.m., Sarena attached the Notice to Take Depositions (NTTD) for the Defendant’s Depositions and noted that a Spanish translator had been requested for the day; she also said she had asked Mrs. Thomas and Sariya to check their availability and would update Londergan as soon as she heard back.

At 11:21 a.m. on February 11, 2025, Londergan informed that Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6, but Ms. Castillo would be available that day. He also indicated that if both depositions were to be conducted on the same day, both Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo would be available on any of these dates: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, or March 27. A conference room at SBMKY’s office would be available on any of these dates, and if none of these dates worked for the opposing office, dates in April could be arranged. He invited further discussion by phone.

Sarena responded on February 11, 2025 at 12:59 p.m., indicating that they could move the deposition to March 13 without issue. Matthew replied later that day at 1:22 p.m., saying they would inform their clients. Earlier in the thread, the initial note had stated that the depositions were to begin March 6, 2025 with Vilches and continue with the other party, with the possibility of rescheduling if needed.

In sum, the deposition plan involved coordinating the depositions of Mrs. Vilches and Mrs. Castillo around early March 2025, with contingencies for May/April dates if necessary, a Spanish translator for the day, and a conference-room venue. On February 11, 2025, it was noted that Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available on March 18, 2025, adding to the schedule of potential dates and confirming continued communication among all counsel.

item_50.note: This narrative summarizes the email communications and scheduling discussions between The Whaley Law Firm and SBMKY Law Firm, dated February 7 through March 13, 2025, concerning the deposition planning for Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo et al. in the Jeff Cir Court, case number 23-CI-006039, with Sariya Mason as the client.

On February 7, 2025 at 3:38 PM, Matthew R. Londergan (Attorney, SBMKY Law) informed Bryce that both clients are available on several dates: Thursday, February 20 after 11 a.m.; Thursday, March 6 any time; Thursday, March 13 any time; and Thursday, March 27 any time. He noted that a Spanish interpreter would be needed for these depositions and that Thursdays generally work best; if the listed dates did not work, they would obtain additional dates. His contact details were provided, and a confidentiality notice accompanied the message.

On February 9 or 10, 2025, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm replied. In a message sent at 9:46 AM on February 10, she stated that March 6, 2025, beginning at 10:00 a.m., would work for their office, with Ms. Vilches first and Ms. Castillo in the afternoon, or vice versa; she asked whether they could use the sending office for the depositions to accommodate the parties. Her signature included her title, the firm’s address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, and her direct line. A confidentiality notice was included in the email.

Later on February 10, 2025 at 11:04 AM, Sarena responded again: “Awesome, sounds great. We will get a notice over to you & the court reporter today,” reaffirming the plan and indicating they would issue the deposition notice to both the opposing party and the court reporter. This email also carried the standard confidentiality notice.

At 11:16 AM on February 10, 2025, Matthew Londergan replied that they would like to schedule his clients’ depositions in the same timeframe and asked Sarena to send dates when Ms. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available in March or April. His message included his office address at 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, KY 40202, and his direct contact numbers, along with the confidentiality notice.

In a follow-up at 11:23 AM on February 10, 2025, Sarena sent the email with the attached NTTD (Notice to Take Depositions) for the defendants’ depositions and noted that they had requested a Spanish translator for the day. She also stated she had sent a request to Mrs. Thomas and Sariya Mason to check their availability and that she would update SBMKY as soon as she heard back. Her signature block again listed The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information and new email address.

Sarena’s earlier message from February 10, 2025 at 11:04 AM was preceded by an earlier note stating, “Awesome, sounds great. We will get a notice over to you & the court reporter today,” confirming that a notice would be issued promptly.

On February 10, 2025 at 9:46 AM, Sarena had proposed the detailed schedule for March 6, 2025: beginning at 10:00 a.m. with Mrs. Vilches and continuing with Mrs. Castillo in the afternoon, or the order could be reversed; she asked whether it would be acceptable to use The Whaley Law Firm’s office for the depositions to facilitate the process.

By February 11, 2025 at 11:21 AM, Matthew informed Sarena that they had learned Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6. Ms. Castillo remained available on that day, but if the parties preferred to conduct both depositions on the same day, they had confirmed that both Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo would be available on any of the following days: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, and March 27. They also noted that a conference room was available at their office for the depositions on any of these dates, and they offered to arrange dates in April if none of the listed dates worked for the other side. He concluded by inviting a discussion over the phone if needed. His signature block again provided his office details: 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, KY 40202, with direct phone and fax numbers and the confidentiality notice.

Later on February 11, 2025 at 12:58:38 PM, Sarena replied to Matthew: “Good afternoon Matt, Thank you for the update & dates. We can move it to the 13th without an issue.” She confirmed acceptance of the proposed March 13 date and repeated that they could shift to that date given the updated availability, and she provided her contact details, including her new email address at The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with direct lines and email. The message itself did not include any additional scheduling details beyond confirming the March 13 option, but it did reiterate the shift to that date and acknowledged the update.

Across these exchanges, several consistent points appear: the depositions pertain to the Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo et al. matter in Jeff Cir Court, case 23-CI-006039; the clients involved include Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo, with Ms. Thomas and Sariya Mason also mentioned for scheduling; a Spanish interpreter has been requested for the deposition day; The Whaley Law Firm offered use of its office space (including a conference room) to accommodate the depositions; the parties discussed scheduling across several potential dates, primarily in March 2025, with some consideration of April if needed; and the communications repeatedly included confidentiality notices and standard firm contact information, including the firm’s address, phone numbers, and Sarena’s new email address.

In sum, the correspondence documents a coordinated effort in February 2025 to schedule the depositions of the involved parties, balancing the availability of Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo, arranging for a Spanish translator, securing a conference room, and aligning dates so that the depositions for these related matters could be conducted efficiently, ultimately confirming March 13, 2025 as a feasible date for the depositions with permission to proceed on that day.

item_51.note: Case overview: This note concerns the Sariya Mason client (Sariya Mason, DB [DOB-204]) in Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo et al.,Jefferson Circuit Court, case number 23-CI-006039.

Chronology of communications:

- January 24, 2025: Bryce Koon, Esq., on behalf of The Whaley Law Firm, emailed Deanna M. Tucker, Kristy M. King, Matthew Londergan, and others (including a Filevine project address for Sariya Mason) requesting dates in February or March for the depositions. The message was a general follow-up requesting deposition dates.

- February 7, 2025, 3:38 PM: Matthew R. Londergan, attorney, replied with potential deposition dates for both clients: Thursday, February 20 after 11 a.m.; Thursday, March 6 any time; Thursday, March 13 any time; Thursday, March 27 any time. He noted that a Spanish interpreter would be required for these depositions and invited Bryce to advise if these dates did not work to obtain additional options, adding that Thursdays generally work best for their clients.

- February 9, 2025, 9:46 AM: Sarena M. Tuttle, litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm, responded to Matthew. She proposed March 6, 2025 beginning at 10:00 a.m. with Mrs. Vilches and continuing with Mrs. Castillo in the afternoon or vice versa, and asked consent to use the firm’s office for the convenience of the parties.

- February 10, 2025, 10:24 AM: Matthew replied that the conference room at their office would be available that day and that the depositions could proceed in either order.

- February 10, 2025, 11:04 AM: Sarena responded, “Awesome, sounds great. We will get a notice over to you & the court reporter today,” confirming next steps.

- February 10, 2025, 11:16 AM: Matthew followed up, stating the desire to schedule the depositions for both clients in the same timeframe and requesting that Sarena send dates when Ms. Thomas and Sariya Mason would be available in March/April.

- February 10, 2025, 11:23 AM: Sarena sent a reply with the NTTD (Notice to Take Deposition) for the Defendant’s Depositions attached. She noted that a Spanish translator had been requested and that she had sent a request to Mrs. Thomas and Sariya to check availability, promising to provide an update once responses were received.

- February 11, 2025, 4:21 PM (UTC): Matthew Londergan sent an update indicating new scheduling constraints: they had learned that Ms. Vilches would be out of the country on March 6, but Ms. Castillo would still be available that day. To accommodate either schedule, he proposed that, if the parties preferred to depose both witnesses on the same day, both Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo would be available at any time on one of the following alternative dates: March 13, March 18, March 20, March 25, or March 27. He also confirmed that a conference room at their office would be available for the depositions on any of these dates. If none of these dates work for the opponent, they would pursue dates in April. He closed by inviting a call to discuss further.

Other notes and identifiers:
- The case caption remains Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo et al., Jeff Cir Court, 23-CI-006039.
- The client involved in this matter is Sariya Mason (DB [DOB-1210]).
- The parties identified for deposition include Ms. Vilches, Ms. Castillo, and involvement of Ms. Thomas and Sariya Mason.
- A Spanish interpreter is required for these depositions.
- The depositions were proposed to be held at the Whaley Law Firm office, with a conference room reserved for convenience.
- The communications included a series of confirmations, notices to court reporters, and requests to check availability, with a standing offer to adjust dates into April if needed.
- Contact details for the participants include:
  - Matthew R. Londergan, Attorney, 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, KY 40202. Direct Phone: [PHONE-206]; Direct Fax: [PHONE-1208].
  - Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222. Direct Phone: [PHONE-1207]; Office: [PHONE-209] ext 104; Email: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (new address noted).
- In the email footnotes, confidentiality notices were included in each message, indicating the communications are privileged and intended only for the named recipients.

In summary, the parties are coordinating deposition dates for Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo et al., with a plan to depoise Ms. Vilches and Ms. Castillo (and possibly Ms. Thomas and Sariya Mason) around mid-to-late March, considering March 13, 18, 20, 25, or 27 as potential options if March 6 proves infeasible due to Ms. Vilches’ travel. A Spanish translator was requested, and a court-notice to the court reporter was planned. The Whaley Law Firm offered their conference room for the depositions and remains open to adjusting to April if needed.

item_53.note: In the Schrice Thomas v Yanelys Castillo et al. case (Jeff Cir Crt - 23-CI-006039), the structured correspondence between The Whaley Law Firm and SBMKY Law concerns scheduling depositions for the clients Mrs. Vilches and Mrs. Castillo. The client listed in the file is Sariya Mason, with the case reference Sariya Mason DB [DOB-213] in Filevine.

The first relevant note begins with an email chain from January 9, 2025, when Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, advised counsel that all written discovery had been completed or was near completion. She requested that the deposition of Mrs. Vilches be scheduled as soon as possible and asked that both sides provide dates when they and their clients would be available. Because Mrs. Vilches’ native language is not English, Sarena also asked that a translator be arranged and that the native language of Mrs. Vilches be confirmed to ensure proper scheduling.

A follow-up from January 17, 2025 reiterates the scheduling request for Mrs. Vilches’s deposition and adds that Mrs. Vilches speaks some derivative of Spanish. Sarena requested confirmation of Mrs. Vilches’s native language to determine the best translator. She also noted that the claim is more than 2.5 years old and emphasizes the existence of video footage showing an unprovoked attack, suggesting that a Zoom deposition might be preferable though not ideal. She urged prompt scheduling and invited any questions to be discussed directly.

On January 24, 2025, Bryce Koon, counsel for The Whaley Law Firm, responded to the scheduling requests. He stated that they were again attempting to obtain dates for the client depositions and asked for dates in February or March when the depositions could be conducted. The message was addressed to Deanna M. Tucker and Kristy M. King and copied to Sarena Tuttle and the Sariya Mason DB [DOB-214] Filevine project email address. The correspondence included standard confidentiality language indicating it was intended only for the named recipients and warning against disclosure if received in error.

Following that, on February 7, 2025, Matthew Londergan of SBMKY Law replied to Bryce and others. He apologized for the delay and stated that both of their clients were available on several dates: Thursday, February 20 after 11 a.m.; Thursday, March 6 any time; Thursday, March 13 any time; and Thursday, March 27 any time. He also confirmed that a Spanish interpreter would be required for the depositions. He invited colleagues to flag any conflicts with those dates and offered to obtain additional options if needed. His message also included his standard attorney contact details and confidentiality notice.

On February 10, 2025, Sarena Tuttle replied with a proposed deposition plan. She wrote that March 6, 2025, beginning at 10:00 a.m., with Mrs. Vilches, and continuing with Mrs. Castillo in the afternoon (or vice versa) would work for The Whaley Law Firm. She asked Matthew Londergan whether they could use his office for the convenience of the parties.

That same day, February 10, 2025, at 3:24 p.m., Matthew Londergan confirmed that the conference room at their office would be available on the requested day, and he noted that the depositions could proceed in either order depending on what the parties preferred. He provided his direct phone and fax numbers and included his firm’s confidentiality notice. He also shared the firm’s address: 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, Kentucky 40202.

In summary, the depositions for Mrs. Vilches and Mrs. Castillo were being coordinated with a plan to hold them on March 6, 2025, starting at 10:00 a.m., in the conference room at SBMKY Law’s Louisville office, with flexibility regarding the order of the two depositions and the use of a Spanish interpreter to accommodate language needs. The parties also considered the possibility of conducting a Zoom deposition if necessary, given the age of the case and the existence of video footage of the incident.

item_60.note: In the matter of Schrice Thomas v. Yanelys Castillo et al., Jefferson Circuit Court Case 23-CI-006039, the depositions of the witnesses were coordinated across a long email thread in early 2025. The client listed in the structured file is Sariya Mason (case file: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-249]). The thread shows ongoing discussions between The Whaley Law Firm and SBMKY Law about scheduling depositions for Ms. Thomas and Ms. Mason, with a particular focus on the witnesses Mrs. Vilches and Mrs. Castillo, and with a Spanish interpreter required.

The exchange began with an email from January 9, 2025. Sarena Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, asked Matthew Londergan, an attorney at SBMKY Law, to schedule the deposition of Mrs. Vilches as soon as possible. She requested confirmation of Mrs. Vilches’s native language to ensure an appropriate translator could be arranged, noting that the language was not English and that scheduling would hinge on identifying the best translator for Mrs. Vilches.

On January 17, 2025, Sarena followed up, indicating that March 6, 2025, beginning at 10:00 a.m., would work for her office for the deposition of Mrs. Vilches, with the deposition of Mrs. Castillo to follow in the afternoon or vice versa. She also suggested using SBMKY’s office for the convenience of the parties and asked for confirmation of the native language to ensure proper translation arrangements. Her message also referenced that the claim in question is more than two and a half years old and included video footage of the incident, described as an unprovoked attack, underscoring the time sensitivity of scheduling and translation needs.

On January 24, 2025, Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm emailed counsel, reiterating the need to obtain deposition dates and requesting dates in February or March for both sides’ clients. He CC’d Sarena Tuttle and included Sariya Mason’s filehouse contact as part of the Filevine project.

On February 7, 2025, Matthew Londergan replied to Bryce, listing several potential dates: Thursday, February 20 after 11 a.m.; Thursday, March 6 (any time); Thursday, March 13 (any time); and Thursday, March 27 (any time). He noted that both clients would require a Spanish interpreter and welcomed additional date suggestions if these did not work, adding that Thursdays generally work best for their clients.

The thread continued on February 9 and February 10, 2025, with further scheduling details. On February 10 at 9:46 a.m., Sarena Tuttle responded that March 6, 2025, beginning at 10:00 a.m., would work for her office for the deposition of Mrs. Vilches, with Mrs. Castillo to be scheduled for the afternoon or vice versa. She asked whether SBMKY would allow the deposition to be held at The Whaley Law Firm’s office for the convenience of the parties and reiterated the need to confirm Mrs. Vilches’s native language to arrange a translator.

Shortly after, at 10:24 a.m. on February 10, Matthew Londergan confirmed that the conference room at SBMKY’s office would be available on that day and that the deposition order could be arranged to suit the parties’ preferences. He indicated that the depositions could be conducted in SBMKY’s conference room and that the order of the two depositions could be arranged to accommodate the witnesses.

Later on February 10, 2025, at 11:04 a.m., Sarena wrote that she would send a notice to both the opposing counsel and the court reporter that day. She reaffirmed the confidentiality of the communication, as did the standard notices that accompanied the email chain.

Finally, at 4:16 p.m. (UTC) on February 10, 2025, Matthew Londergan sent a concluding note reiterating the request to schedule the depositions within the same timeframe and asking Sarena to provide dates in March or April when Ms. Thomas and Sariya Mason could be available. He closed with his standard attorney signature block, including his office address at 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, Kentucky 40202, direct phone number [PHONE-250], and direct fax [PHONE-251].

Throughout these correspondences, confidentiality notices were included in each message, reminding recipients that the communications and any attachments are intended for the named parties and may be privileged. The exchanges show a collaborative effort to coordinate two depositions (Ms. Vilches and Mrs. Castillo) in the JeffCir Crt case, with a strong emphasis on securing a Spanish interpreter and choosing a scheduling window that aligns with both sides’ availability in March and April, ideally within SBMKY’s conference room for convenience. The Whaley Law Firm’s contact details were consistently provided, including Sarena Tuttle’s role as a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager, and her new email address.

On January 9, 2025, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, wrote that, after reviewing the file, all written discovery had been completed and/or was near completion. item_101.note: In the matter of Thomas v. Castillo, within the Sariya-Mason file (Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-476]) for client Sariya Mason, an email chain in late November and early December 2024 covered discovery responses and extension requests. The primary participants were Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm; Deanna M. Tucker, Partner at SBM Kentucky Law; Kristy M. King, Legal Assistant at SBM Kentucky Law; and colleagues Aaron Whaley and Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm.

On December 2, 2024, at 3:12 PM, Sarena sent a note to Deanna Tucker with copies to Kristy King and others, acknowledging an extension request that had been noted for December 6. Sarena stated she could grant only a two-week extension, which would fall on a holiday Friday, and she expressed understanding that papers would not be received on that day. She closed by noting her new contact information.

Earlier that same day, at 2:57 PM, Deanna Tucker replied, acknowledging that Friday had been a court holiday and indicating that they would serve the documents that day. The message included Deanna’s standard contact details and confidentiality notice.

Also on December 2, at 2:17 PM, Sarena followed up with Kristy King (and Deanna Tucker), asking for an update on the responses and inviting further discussion if needed.

Looking back, on November 20, 2024, Sarena had written that the Supplemental Discovery was originally served on October 18, 2024. She referenced attached email correspondence for context and explained that, while she understood Deanna Tucker’s trial commitments, she could grant an extension to November 29, 2024, with any additional time requiring approval from the attorneys. She added the attorneys to the email chain for review of the extension request.

Earlier, on November 19, 2024, Kristy King replied that she had received the prior message and noted that Deanna Tucker had been unable to locate the email showing when the materials were sent; Kristy asked for confirmation of the date of service and suggested that, given Tucker’s trial schedule, they would need to request an extension and asked whether December 6 would be agreeable.

That same day, November 19, at 3:35 PM, Sarena responded to Kristy, attaching Word and PDF versions of the requested documents and inviting any further needs.

At 10:38 AM on November 19, 2024, Aaron Whaley forwarded a message from Kristy King requesting a copy of the supplemental discovery requests that accompany the attached Notice of Service, noting that she had not received a copy. Kristy’s message included her contact details and a confidentiality disclaimer.

Kristy King’s earlier message, sent at 7:49 AM on November 19, 2024, had asked for a copy of the supplemental discovery requests that go with the attached Notice of Service, stating that she never received them. Aaron Whaley then forwarded Kristy’s request into the chain, with contact information for himself and Bryce Koon.

Across these exchanges, the parties discussed service dates, potential extensions (including a proposed December 6 extension), the need for attorney approval for extensions beyond November 29, 2024, and the provision of Word and PDF copies of the requested discovery documents. The chain also included confidentiality notices typical of communications among the firms.

item_180.note: This note summarizes a series of communications in the case of Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., Jefferson Circuit Court case 23-CI-006039, involving the client Sariya Mason and the attorney team at The Whaley Law Firm (case file: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-894]). The messages center on discovery, production of documents, and motions, and they track the progression of discovery and related filings through early 2024.

On December 7, 2023, Deanna M. Tucker replied to a message from W. Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm regarding the Sariya Mason matter. Tucker indicated that she had received Bryce’s communications and requested that her legal assistant, Kristy M. King, be copied on emails. Tucker’s message also included a note that she had copies of the materials, and it was part of a thread that included contact with Sarena Tuttle and Kristy King, with all communications cc’d to them. Bryce’s signature on that message shows The Whaley Law Firm’s Louisville, Kentucky office at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with a phone number of [PHONE-895] and a fax of [PHONE-896].

On January 18, 2024, Bryce followed up regarding the discovery work in the case. He stated that, although they had received answers to the requests for admission, the responses to the interrogatories and the production of documents remained outstanding. He emphasized that, while he did not seek unnecessary litigation, if no responses were received by the following week, he would be forced to file a motion to compel the discovery responses.

 Bryce repeated the follow-up theme on January 31, 2024, writing that he was again seeking the outstanding discovery responses and asking for a timeline for their delivery.

In a February 14, 2024 message, Bryce again referenced the ongoing efforts to obtain responses to the interrogatories and production requests, reiterating that they had been attempting to obtain these for some time. He warned that, if they did not hear back within a week, they would be compelled to file a motion to compel. The message again reiterated the intention to move forward if there was no timely response.

On February 21, 2024, Bryce informed counsel that the attached document had been filed and that the matter was set for next Monday’s motion hour, signaling a scheduled hearing related to the discovery issues. His message reiterated the standard Whaley Law Firm closing and included the firm’s signature block with the same Louisville address and contact information.

Meanwhile, on March 25, 2024, Kristy M. King, identified as a Legal Assistant for The Whaley Law Firm, sent a message to Bryce Koon and Deanna M. Tucker, with Sarena Tuttle and Matthew Londergan CC’d. King stated that the attached documents contained Defendant’s discovery responses and document production, and noted that a hard copy would not be mailed unless requested. King’s message also included her direct contact details: 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, Kentucky 40202; Direct Phone: [PHONE-897]; Direct Fax: [PHONE-898]. The email also contained a confidentiality notice typical of attorney communications, underscoring that the content is for the named recipients and may be privileged.

Finally, on April 11, 2024, Bryce Koon sent another communication to counsel, again noting that the attached motion had been filed that day and that it was set for Monday’s motion hour. This message continued the pattern of motion practice related to the discovery issues in the Mason case, with the same general recipients and cc’d parties. Bryce’s message was sent from The Whaley Law Firm at the same Louisville address and contact numbers.

In sum, between December 2023 and April 2024, counsel for Sariya Mason and the defense in Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al. engaged in a back-and-forth regarding discovery responses, with multiple follow-ups from Bryce Koon, a March 2024 transmission of the defendant’s discovery responses and production, and two motions being set for hearing in connection with the discovery disputes (one set for the next Monday following February 21, 2024, and another set for the Monday following April 11, 2024). The communications were distributed among Bryce Koon, Deanna M. Tucker, Kristy M. King, Sarena Tuttle, and Matthew Londergan, with Kristy King formally included as the recipient as of March 25, 2024 and the chain preserving the confidentiality notices customary to such attorney communications.

item_183.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-908]. Client: Sariya Mason. The record documents a sequence of discovery-related communications in the case Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., filed in Jefferson Circuit Court (Jefferson Circuit 23-CI-006039) and carried through spring 2024. The sender in most communications is W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm in Louisville, Kentucky (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-909]; fax [PHONE-910], though an earlier message shows a different fax number). The recipient list includes Deanna M. Tucker of SBMKY Law ([EMAIL-911]) and her co-counsel, Deanna M. Tucker, along with other recipients such as Sarena Tuttle and Kristy M. King. The communications repeatedly reference the discovery responses and document productions associated with the defendant in this matter, as well as the scheduling of motions for their motion hour. Each email contains a confidentiality notice typical of attorney communications.

On December 7, 2023, Deanna M. Tucker replied to Bryce Koon, noting that Bryce should include her legal assistant, Kristy King, on future emails and indicating she had copied Kristy on the exchange. She signed as Deanna M. Tucker, a partner at her firm, with the email signature including her Louisville address and direct contact details. A confidentiality notice accompanied this and related messages.

On January 18, 2024, Bryce followed up again, stating that, although answers to the requests for admission had been received, responses to the interrogatories and the production of documents remained outstanding. He indicated that, while he did not want extraneous litigation, a motion to compel would be pursued if no responses were forthcoming.

The next day, January 31, 2024, Bryce again reached out to Deanna Tucker, asking to be advised when the outstanding discovery responses could be expected. The correspondence continued the theme of pressing for complete discovery.

On February 14, 2024, Bryce sent another message to Deanna Tucker, reiterating that attempts had been ongoing for some time to obtain responses to the interrogatories and requests for production. He warned that if they did not hear back by the following week, they would be compelled to file a motion to compel. This message again carried the standard confidentiality boilerplate.

A subsequent email on February 21, 2024, from Bryce Koon stated that the attached filing had been made that day and was set for the next Monday’s motion hour. The chain notes that this is in the Jefferson Circuit case identified as 23-CI-006039, and the message reiterates the motion-hour scheduling.

On March 25, 2024, Kristy M. King, serving as legal assistant, sent a message to Bryce Koon and Deanna Tucker (with Sarena Tuttle and Matthew Londergan CC’d) reporting that the defendant’s discovery responses and document production were attached. She indicated that a hard copy would not follow by mail unless requested and invited any questions. The message carries a confidentiality notice typical of such communications.

Finally, on April 11, 2024, Bryce Koon sent Good morning emails to counsel stating that the attached motion had been filed that day and was set for Monday’s motion hour. He included a full signature block for The Whaley Law Firm, with the Louisville address and contact information. The record shows the ongoing coordination around the motion and the discovery matters in Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., in Jefferson Circuit Court (23-CI-006039). The April 11 message also includes the standard attorney-confidentiality notices typical of such communications.

In summary, over late 2023 and early to mid-2024, the parties repeatedly corresponded about outstanding discovery responses (interrogatories and document production), with admissions responses already provided, and ongoing efforts culminating in the filing of a motion (and scheduling for the motion hour) in the Jefferson Circuit case 23-CI-006039, all linked to the representation of Sariya Mason by The Whaley Law Firm and the opposing counsel, Deanna M. Tucker of SBMKY Law, along with several supporting staff.

item_185.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-915]
Client: Sariya Mason

Case context:
In the matter of Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., filed in Jefferson Circuit Court (docket number 23-CI-006039), a sequence of discovery communications occurred between counsel at The Whaley Law Firm and counsel at SBM Legal Group. The primary contacts were W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, representing the plaintiff, Sariya Mason, and Deanna M. Tucker, Esq., a partner at SBM, representing the defendant group. Kristy M. King, a legal assistant at SBM, and Sarena Tuttle, and others at the two firms were copied on various communications. The emails repeatedly noted that they contained attorney-client privileged material and were not to be disclosed if received in error.

December 7, 2023 communications:
- At 2:56 PM, Bryce Koon sent an email to Deanna M. Tucker with the subject Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 23-CI-006039). He attached Plaintiff’s First Set of Discovery and the associated notice filed that day and stated that a Word copy was included for convenience. He asked Deanna to contact him with any questions.
- At 3:13 PM, Deanna Tucker replied, noting that Bryce should include her legal assistant, Kristy King, on email communications and that she had copied Kristy on the present email.
- At 3:15 PM, Bryce Koon responded confirming the same, and he continued the thread with the parties and copies as appropriate.

January 2024 follow-up communications:
- January 18, 2024, at 3:18 PM, Bryce Koon sent a follow-up message to Deanna Tucker. He stated that discovery responses had been outstanding, including interrogatories and production of documents, and he requested that Deanna advise when they could be expected. He reiterated that there should be no waiver of privilege and that the messages were intended for the named recipient.
- January 31, 2024, at 1:08 PM, Bryce Koon again followed up with Deanna Tucker, asking for an update on the outstanding discovery responses and when they might be expected.
- January 18 and January 31 messages repeatedly referenced the parties’ ongoing efforts to obtain the plaintiff’s responses (interrogatories and production of documents) and warned that, absent timely responses, a motion to compel could be pursued.

February 2024 prior to the March 2024 disclosure:
- February 7 or early February communications are noted in the record through February 14, 2024, at 4:09 PM. In this message, Bryce Koon stated that they had been attempting to obtain responses for some time and, while not seeking extraneous litigation, if no response was received by the following week, a motion to compel would be filed. He reiterated that the case involved interrogatories and requests for production of documents.
- February 21, 2024, at 4:34 PM, Bryce Koon reported that “today” they had filed something related to the discovery and that the matter was set for next Monday’s motion hour. He signed as counsel for The Whaley Law Firm and included standard attorney-client disclaimers.

March 25, 2024 communication:
- On March 25, 2024, Kristy M. King, Legal Assistant for SBM, sent an email concerning the same case. In this message, she stated that attached were the Defendant’s discovery responses and document production. She noted that a hard copy would not follow by mail unless requested. The email included her contact information (address, direct phone, and direct fax) and bore SBM’s confidentiality notice. The communication was directed to counsel at The Whaley Law Firm (Bryce Koon and Deanna M. Tucker) and copied Sarena Tuttle and Matthew Londergan.

Additional notes:
- The chain repeatedly employed the standard confidentiality language typical of attorney communications, indicating that the messages and attachments were intended for the named recipients and may be privileged; if received in error, recipients were instructed to notify the sender and destroy the materials.
- Throughout the timeline, the subject line for these communications consistently referenced Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 23-CI-006039), and messages circulated among Bryce Koon, Deanna Tucker, Kristy King, Sarena Tuttle, and others at both law firms.
- The March 25, 2024 message confirms the defendant’s discovery responses and document production had been assembled and sent electronically, with a note that a hard copy would not be mailed unless requested.

In summary, from December 2023 through March 2024, the parties engaged in a back-and-forth sequence regarding discovery responses and document production in the Jefferson Circuit case 23-CI-006039, with multiple follow-ups by The Whaley Law Firm indicating delays and potential motions to compel, culminating in a March 25, 2024 email transmitting the defendant’s discovery responses and production and noting no required hard-copy mailing unless requested.

Marzian Tucker, Partner, with the Louisville, Kentucky address and direct contact details, and the message also carried the confidentiality notice.

He advised that the discovery requests had been served and noted that responses had been received for the requests for admission, but that responses to interrogatories and the production of documents remained outstanding. He asked Deanna to advise when those remaining responses could be expected, and he concluded with his standard contact information and confidentiality notice, with Sarena Tuttle and Kristy M. King cc’d on the email.

Finally, on January 31, 2024, at 1:08 p.m., Koon sent another follow-up to Deanna Tucker regarding the outstanding discovery responses. He again requested guidance on when the responses may be expected and closed with his contact information and the confidentiality notice. The CC on this message included Sarena Tuttle and Kristy M. King, and the email carried the subject line RE: Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 23-CI-006039).

Throughout these exchanges, the emails repeatedly contained attorney-client privilege and confidentiality notices, and the sender’s firm information appeared in the signatures: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with phone numbers [PHONE-1003] and fax numbers [PHONE-1004] (and [PHONE-1005] in earlier messages). Surelis Castillo, et al., Jefferson Circuit 23-CI-006039.
