item_213.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-1039]
Client: Sariya Mason

This note summarizes a sequence of email communications in the matter of Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., Jefferson Circuit Court case number 23-CI-006039. The communications involve counsel for the plaintiff, W. Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm, and counsel for the defendants, Deanna M. Tucker. The note traces discovery-related correspondence beginning in December 2023 and continuing through February 2024, culminating in a filing that was attached to an email on February 21, 2024 and set for the following Monday’s motion hour.

On December 7, 2023, Bryce Koon sent an email to Deanna Tucker attaching Plaintiff’s First Set of Discovery and the associated notice filed that day, and he noted that a Word copy was included for convenience. The message contains the standard confidentiality and privilege notices typical of electronic correspondence from counsel, and the Whaley Law Firm’s contact details were included: 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with a phone number of [PHONE-1040] and a fax number listed as [PHONE-1041] in this instance. In the same thread, Deanna Tucker replied later that day (3:13 PM) requesting that her legal assistant, Kristy King, be included on emails, and she provided her own signature with the firm’s confidential notice. Bryce Koon responded shortly thereafter (3:15 PM) confirming that Kristy King would be included on future emails.

Earlier, on January 18, 2024 (3:18 PM), Koon followed up on the discovery requests, noting that responses to the requests for admission had been received, but that the interrogatories and production of documents remained outstanding, and he asked when such responses could be expected. He included his standard firm signature and contact information, with the fax number listed as [PHONE-1042] in this message. The confidentiality and privilege notices were again part of the email footer.

On January 31, 2024, Koon again wrote Deanna Tucker to follow up on the outstanding discovery responses, requesting an update on when they may be expected. The message continued to bear the Whaley Law Firm’s identifying information and the customary confidentiality disclaimer.

On February 14, 2024, Koon sent another reminder, noting that, “as you can see below,” the law firm had been attempting to obtain responses for some time. He stated that if they did not hear back by the following week, they would be forced to file a motion to compel regarding discovery responses. This message again carried his standard signature and the confidentiality notice.

Finally, on February 21, 2024, Koon sent a good-afternoon counsel email informing Deanna Tucker that the attached filing had been filed that day and was set for the next Monday’s motion hour. The message indicates that the filing was associated with the Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo matter, and it reiterates the ongoing scheduling of a motion hour. The February 21 email also lists the same recipients as in prior messages, with Deanna Tucker as the primary recipient and Sarena Tuttle and Kristy M. King CC’d. The signature again identifies The Whaley Law Firm and provides the Louisville address, the phone line, and the fax line (this time listing the fax as [PHONE-1043]). As with the prior messages, the email includes the standard confidentiality and privilege notices.

Across the chain, the key facts include: the case caption and docket number of Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, Jefferson Circuit, 23-CI-006039; the plaintiff’s first set of discovery and accompanying notice filed December 7, 2023; ongoing discovery responses (specifically, admitted responses obtained, but interrogatories and production of documents still outstanding); repeated follow-ups from counsel requesting prompt production of these documents and responses; and the intent to seek relief by way of a motion to compel if responses were not forthcoming by the stated deadlines. The communications also show a routine practice of including Kristy M. King, Deanna Tucker’s assistant, on correspondence and the use of standard client-attorney privilege and confidentiality notices in each email.

The Whaley Law Firm’s contact details appear in the signature blocks across the messages, with the Louisville, Kentucky address of 712 Lyndon Lane, 40222, a landline of [PHONE-1044], and the fax number varying between [PHONE-1045] in December 2023 messages and [PHONE-1046] in later messages (including the February 21, 2024 email). Deanna Tucker’s communications from this period also included a confidentiality notice and her role as a partner at the firm located at 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, KY 40202, with direct phone [PHONE-1047] and direct fax [PHONE-1048].

In summary, this case has a documented history of discovery activity beginning with the December 2023 filing of the plaintiff’s first set of discovery, followed by a series of communications pressing for timely responses to interrogatories and production requests, and culminating in a February 21, 2024 email announcing a filed filing and a scheduled motion hour for the following Monday. The exchange reflects ongoing efforts to resolve discovery disputes with the potential for a motion to compel if timely responses were not provided.

item_214.note: The case is Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., Jefferson Circuit Court case 23-CI-006039, with the matter labeled as Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-1050] in the file. The client in this matter is Sariya Mason. The correspondence summarized below occurred between The Whaley Law Firm and SBMK Law, involving counsel W. Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm and Deanna M. Tucker (apparently a partner at SBMK).

On December 7, 2023, Bryce Koon sent an email to Deanna M. Tucker attaching Plaintiff’s First Set of Discovery and the associated notice filed that day; a Word copy was included for convenience. He stated that if there were any questions, Deanna should let him know. The message was sent from The Whaley Law Firm, located at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with the firm’s phone number [PHONE-1051] and fax [PHONE-1052]. The email carried the standard confidentiality notice applicable to electronic communications, and it identified the recipient as Deanna M. Tucker.

In a reply later the same day, December 7, 2023 at 3:13 PM, Deanna M. Tucker replied that Bryce should include her legal assistant, Kristy King, on emails and that she had copied Kristy on the email. She signed as Deanna M. Marzian Tucker, Partner, with the SBMK address at 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, Kentucky 40202. Her direct phone was [PHONE-1053] and direct fax [PHONE-1054]. A confidentiality notice followed, reiterating privilege and the need to destroy or forward communications only to the intended recipient if there was an error in transmission.

Shortly after, at 3:15 PM on December 7, 2023, Bryce Koon replied, “Will do,” indicating he would include Kristy King on future emails. The communication again carried the Whaley Law Firm contact details and the same confidentiality notice.

On January 18, 2024, Bryce Koon again wrote to Deanna M. Tucker. He noted that he was following up on the discovery requests served in this matter and observed that answers had been received for the requests for admission, but the responses to interrogatories and the production of documents remained outstanding. He requested that Deanna advise when the remaining responses could be expected. The message again included the Whaley Law Firm contact information and a confidentiality notice.

On January 31, 2024, Bryce Koon sent another follow-up email to Deanna M. Tucker, reiterating the outstanding discovery responses and asking Deanna to advise when they may be expected. The notice and contact details remained the same, with the confidentiality disclaimer.

Finally, on February 14, 2024, Bryce Koon sent a further forward-looking message to Deanna M. Tucker, copied to Sarena Tuttle of the Whaley Law Firm and Kristy M. King of SBMK. He stated that, as shown below, they had been attempting for some time to obtain responses to the interrogatories and requests for production of documents that had previously been served. He noted that he did not wish for extraneous litigation, but warned that if they did not receive a response by this time next week, they would be forced to file a motion to compel in this regard. The message, like the others, included the standard confidentiality notice and The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information.

Throughout the correspondence, the involved offices were The Whaley Law Firm (Bryce Koon, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-1055]; fax [PHONE-1056]) and SBMK Law (Deanna M. Tucker, Kristy M. King as requested), with Deanna’s affiliation and contact information provided in her reply of December 7, 2023. The emails repeatedly carry the confidentiality notices typical of attorney communications and reflect ongoing discovery practice in the Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo case.

item_215.note: Case: Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 23-CI-006039). Client: Sariya Mason. This narrative summarizes the email correspondence between counsel handling the matter and traces discovery and motion scheduling activity in the case.

On February 21, 2024, at 16:33:49 (UTC-05:00), W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to Deanna M. Tucker, Esq., with copies to Sarena Tuttle and Kristy M. King. He stated, “Good afternoon counsel, Please see attached filed today and set for next Monday’s motion hour.” The message included Koon’s contact information for The Whaley Law Firm—712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, phone [PHONE-1058], fax [PHONE-1059]—and a standard attorney-client privilege confidentiality notice indicating the message is intended only for the named recipient and warning against sharing or using the information if received in error. The same day, the thread shows the ongoing pattern of discovery-related communications between the parties, with the expectation that the attached filing would be addressed during the upcoming motion hour the following Monday.

Earlier in the chain, on February 14, 2024, at 16:09 (UTC-05:00), Koon wrote to Deanna M. Tucker, stating, “As you can see below, we have been attempting for some time now to obtain responses to the interrogatories and requests for production of documents we previously served. While I do not wish for any extraneous litigation, if we do not hear back from you by this time next week we will be forced to file a motion to compel in this regard.” He concluded with his standard firm signature and confidentiality notice.

The record also includes an earlier follow-up from January 31, 2024, at 13:08 (UTC-05:00), in which Koon wrote, “Good afternoon Deanna, I am writing to again follow up on the outstanding discovery responses. Please advise when these may be expected.” The January 31 message was accompanied by Koon’s firm contact details and the usual confidentiality language.

Prior to that, on January 18, 2024, at 15:18 (UTC-05:00), Koon sent a message: “Good afternoon Deanna, Just wanted to follow up on the discovery requests served in this regard. It appears we have received answers to the requests for admission but the responses to interrogatories and production of documents remain outstanding. Please advise when we may expect such responses.” The message again carried Koon’s signature and confidentiality notice.

The chain includes December 7, 2023, at 3:15 PM, in which Koon replied simply, “Will do.” The preceding December 7, 2023, at 3:13 PM, shows Deanna M. Tucker replying to Bryce Koon, requesting that her legal assistant, Kristy King, be included on emails and noting that she had copied Kristy on the email.

Earlier still, on December 7, 2023, at 2:56 PM, Koon wrote, “Attached please find Plaintiff’s First Set of Discovery and the associated notice filed today. A word copy is included for your convenience. If you have any questions, please let me know.” The email carried The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information and the standard confidentiality boilerplate.

In December 2023, Deanna M. Tucker’s reply — dated December 7, 2023 at 3:13 PM — confirmed receipt and requested that her legal assistant, Kristy King, be included on emails, noting she had copied Kristy on the current exchange and reiterating confidentiality of the communications.

Across these exchanges, the central issues have been discovery-related: the plaintiffs’ counsel (W. Bryce Koon, Esq.) has been seeking responses to interrogatories and requests for production of documents, with explicit reminders that failure to respond could lead to a motion to compel; the record also shows that the plaintiff filed a First Set of Discovery, including a notice, in December 2023, and that communications continued into February 2024 regarding the status of discovery responses and scheduling of motions.

This case concerns Sariya Mason as the plaintiff against Surelis Castillo and others, in Jefferson County Circuit Court, docket 23-CI-006039. The parties’ correspondence reflects ongoing discovery efforts and the procedural step of setting a motion hour for a forthcoming filing, with multiple follow-ups aimed at obtaining timely responses to discovery requests and avoiding unnecessary litigation through proactive resolution of discovery disputes.

The series of emails began with a December 7, 2023 message from W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-1062]; fax [PHONE-1063]). In that message, he attached Plaintiff’s First Set of Discovery and the notice filed that day, noting that a Word copy was included for the recipient’s convenience and inviting any questions. The message was sent to Deanna M. Tucker, with a copy to Sarena Tuttle and Kristy M. King, and the subject line identified the case. The body of the email stated, “Attached please find Plaintiff’s First Set of Discovery and the associated notice filed today. A word copy is included for your convenience. If you have any questions, please let me know.” The message included the standard attorney-client/privilege disclaimers common to electronic correspondence.

Shortly thereafter, at 3:13 PM on December 7, 2023, Deanna M. Tucker replied. She asked that Bryce please include her legal assistant, Kristy King, on emails and noted that she had copied Kristy on the exchange. The signature block identified Tucker as a partner located at 401 West Main Street, Suite 1600, Louisville, Kentucky 40202, with direct phone [PHONE-1064] and direct fax [PHONE-1065]. The message also contained a confidentiality notice, indicating the communication and any attachments were intended only for the recipient(s) named and may be subject to attorney-client and/or work product privileges.

Later the same afternoon, at 3:15 PM, Bryce Koon replied, indicating “Will do.” The exchange at that time carried the same general subject matter and the same discovery documents and intent.

On January 18, 2024, at 3:18 PM, Bryce Koon again followed up with Deanna Tucker regarding the discovery requests. He noted that, while answers to the requests for admission appeared to have been received, responses to the interrogatories and to the production of documents remained outstanding, and he asked when those responses could be expected. The message again carried the standard confidentiality disclaimer.

A few days later, on January 31, 2024, at 1:08 PM, Koon sent another follow-up. He stated he was writing to again pursue the outstanding discovery responses and asked Deanna Tucker to advise when those responses may be expected. The note included the attorney’s contact information and the same confidential-disclaimer language.

Then, on February 14, 2024, at 4:09 PM, Koon sent a final follow-up to counsel. He acknowledged that the parties had been attempting for some time to obtain responses to the interrogatories and the requests for production of documents previously served. He stated that, while he did not wish to engage in extraneous litigation, if there was no response by this time next week, they would be forced to file a motion to compel in this regard. The message again included The Whaley Law Firm’s professional contact information and the standard confidentiality notice.

Throughout the correspondence, the communications repeatedly reference the same active matter: Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., Jefferson Circuit Court, case number 23-CI-006039. The note reflects ongoing efforts to obtain full discovery responses (interrogatories and production of documents), with occasional partial responses (notably admissions) and repeated follow-ups over a period extending from December 2023 through February 2024. The law firm contact details for The Whaley Law Firm (Bryce Koon, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-1066]; fax [PHONE-1067]) appear in the December 7, 2023 and February 14, 2024 messages. Deanna M. Tucker’s responses consistently indicate the need to include her legal assistant (Kristy M. King) on communications, a request Tucker conveyed in her December 7, 2023 reply.

In sum, the record shows a back-and-forth sequence of discovery-related emails beginning with the December 7, 2023 transmission of Plaintiff’s First Set of Discovery, followed by multiple follow-ups in January 2024 and a further reminder in February 2024, with counsel warning of a possible motion to compel if the outstanding interrogatories and document productions are not addressed within a stated timeframe.

item_217.note: Case: Sariya-Mason-DB-[DOB-1069]. Client: Sariya Mason. This note documents discovery communications in the matter Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., Jefferson Circuit Court case number 23-CI-006039.

The communications originate from W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm in Louisville, Kentucky, and were sent to Deanna M. Tucker (with several colleagues copied) over a period spanning December 2023 to January 2024. The file shows a consistent pattern of follow-up on outstanding discovery responses in the Jefferson County case.

On December 7, 2023, Bryce Koon emailed Deanna Tucker to transmit Plaintiff’s First Set of Discovery and the associated notice filed that day. He advised that a Word copy of the discovery material was included for convenience and asked counsel to review and let him know if there were any questions. Finally, on January 31, 2024, Bryce Koon sent another concise follow-up to Deanna Tucker. This email again carried the standard Whaley Law Firm signature block and confidentiality notice.

Across the thread, the communications consistently reference the case caption Sariya Mason v. Surelis Castillo, et al., Jefferson Circuit Court case 23-CI-006039. The correspondence also reflects standard attorney‑client privilege notices and the practice of including Kristy M. King, Deanna Tucker’s requested legal assistant, on email communications. There are three vehicles at the animal's residence, indicating the animal should not have been unattended. The client's guardian can be heard yelling at the animal until it returns to its porch. The owners do not seem to respond to the commotion outside, and the animal continues to run loose until the end of the video. Evidence: Video Footage.
